Most of these areas are prone to flash flooding and as such they are often closed according to weather conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1o_Grande" title="Ba\xc3\xb1o Grande">Ba\xc3\xb1o Grande</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1o_de_Oro" title="Ba\xc3\xb1o de Oro">Ba\xc3\xb1o de Oro</a> are two former swimming pools and recreational areas popular between the 1930s and 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These manmade pools were built by the <a href="/wiki/Civilian_Conservation_Corps" title="Civilian Conservation Corps">Civilian Conservation Corps</a> during the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> era by damming creeks belonging to the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Mina_(R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Mina (R\xc3\xado Grande, Puerto Rico)">La Mina River</a> watershed. They were closed due to a series of drownings and other safety issues. Although swimming is no longer possible at these pools, they are preserved as historic sites and have been listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> due to their historic and architectural value since 2017 and 2020, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:13_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ba\xc3\xb1o de Oro now serves as a watershed garden and Ba\xc3\xb1o Grande is now a popular scenic spot.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="El_Portal_Rainforest_Center">El Portal Rainforest Center</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Yunque_National_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: El Portal Rainforest Center"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1237032888/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner img{background-color:white}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner img{background-color:white}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Portal_Rainforest_Center,_central_space.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg/200px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="125" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg/300px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg/400px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center%2C_central_space.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="300" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">El Portal Rainforest Center</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/200px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/400px-El_Portal_Rainforest_Center_of_El_Yunque_National_Forest_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">El Portal Rainforest Center of El Yunque National Forest in Puerto Rico</div></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Opened in 1996, the El Portal Rainforest Center was designed by <a href="/wiki/Segundo_Cardona" title="Segundo Cardona">Segundo Cardona</a>, FAIA of <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Cardona_Ferrer" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Cardona Ferrer">Sierra Cardona Ferrer</a> Architects to give visitors an introduction to what the rainforest looks like. \nBuilt on a 28,434-acre tropical forest, the Portal was built as a model headquarters for ecotourism and economic development and training, the center was built to educate those concerned about the wellbeing of the Caribbean National Forest and preserve the unique tropical forest heritage and environment.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located within the national forest in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Grande, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Grande</a>.\n</p><p>A walkway set at 60 feet (18&#160;m) above the ground allows for a view of the tops of trees, and another walkway winds along tree bases. Exhibits at the center focus on the plants and animals of the rainforest, the importance of rainforests around the world, and threats to rainforests and efforts to conserve them.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The entry experience begins atop an elevated walkway that unites the facility with the surrounding forest and provides views to the mountain peaks, ocean and reforested terrain. The Center contains 9,000 square feet of exhibits, an enclosed theater, conference center classrooms and laboratories, as well as administrative offices. To preserve natural conditions, care was taken to use existing openings for roads, parking areas and buildings while the arrival sequence and parking lots were designed with contours to save existing trees.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The Portal has survived several major hurricanes including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a>. On September 21, 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on caused major damages to the center and renovations are underway as of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> El Portal Rainforest Center reopened to visitors in January 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Yunque_National_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>El Yunque National Forest has been incorrectly called the only rainforest in the United States National Forest Service,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but it is actually the only tropical rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-elyunque_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elyunque-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are others that are temperate rainforests including some in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002, the U.S. Congress designated areas bounded by the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Mameyes" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Mameyes">R\xc3\xado Mameyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Mina_(R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado de la Mina (R\xc3\xado Grande, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado de la Mina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Icacos" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Icacos">R\xc3\xado Icacos</a> in the Caribbean National Forest as components of the <a href="/wiki/National_Wild_and_Scenic_Rivers_System" title="National Wild and Scenic Rivers System">National Wild and Scenic Rivers System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Contrary to the popular assumption, <a href="/wiki/El_Yunque_(Puerto_Rico)" title="El Yunque (Puerto Rico)">El Yunque</a> Peak is not the highest mountain in either the Sierra de Luquillo or Puerto Rico. The highest mountain of the Sierra de Luquillo is <a href="/wiki/El_Toro_(Sierra_de_Luquillo)" title="El Toro (Sierra de Luquillo)">El Toro</a>, also located in the national forest, while the highest mountain in Puerto Rico is <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> on the border between <a href="/wiki/Jayuya,_Puerto_Rico" title="Jayuya, Puerto Rico">Jayuya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>El Yunque is also the object of Puerto Rican folklore and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Culture of Puerto Rico">pop culture</a>. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Coqu%C3%AD" title="Coqu\xc3\xad">coqui</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_amazon" title="Puerto Rican amazon">Puerto Rican parrot</a>, El Yunque is considered a symbol of Puerto Rico and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Ricans</a>. Along with the former two, it was chosen to be Puerto Rico\'s entry in the <a href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful_Quarters" class="mw-redirect" title="America the Beautiful Quarters">America the Beautiful Quarters</a> program. Puerto Rico\'s only <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> site, <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_National_Historic_Site" title="San Juan National Historic Site">San Juan National Historic Site</a> had already been featured on the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_and_United_States_Territories_Quarters" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia and United States Territories Quarters">District of Columbia and United States Territories Quarters</a> in 2009.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Gallery">Gallery</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Yunque_National_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section:
